       2                 :            :  *
       3                 :            :  * execMain.c
       4                 :            :  *        top level executor interface routines
       5                 :            :  *
       6                 :            :  * INTERFACE ROUTINES
       7                 :            :  *      ExecutorStart()
       8                 :            :  *      ExecutorRun()
       9                 :            :  *      ExecutorEnd()
      10                 :            :  *
      11                 :            :  *      The old ExecutorMain() has been replaced by ExecutorStart(),
      12                 :            :  *      ExecutorRun() and ExecutorEnd()
      13                 :            :  *
      14                 :            :  *      These three procedures are the external interfaces to the executor.
      15                 :            :  *      In each case, the query descriptor is required as an argument.
      16                 :            :  *
      17                 :            :  *      ExecutorStart() must be called at the beginning of execution of any
      18                 :            :  *      query plan and ExecutorEnd() should always be called at the end of
      19                 :            :  *      execution of a plan.
      20                 :            :  *
      21                 :            :  *      ExecutorRun accepts direction and count arguments that specify whether
      22                 :            :  *      the plan is to be executed forwards, backwards, and for how many tuples.
      23                 :            :  *
      24                 :            :  * Portions Copyright (c) 2005-2010, Greenplum inc

    2405                 :            : /*
    2406                 :            :  *              ExecContextForcesOids
    2407                 :            :  *
    2408                 :            :  * This is pretty grotty: when doing INSERT, UPDATE, or SELECT INTO,
    2409                 :            :  * we need to ensure that result tuples have space for an OID iff they are
    2410                 :            :  * going to be stored into a relation that has OIDs.  In other contexts
    2411                 :            :  * we are free to choose whether to leave space for OIDs in result tuples
    2412                 :            :  * (we generally don't want to, but we do if a physical-tlist optimization
    2413                 :            :  * is possible).  This routine checks the plan context and returns TRUE if the
    2414                 :            :  * choice is forced, FALSE if the choice is not forced.  In the TRUE case,
    2415                 :            :  * *hasoids is set to the required value.
    2416                 :            :  *
    2417                 :            :  * One reason this is ugly is that all plan nodes in the plan tree will emit
    2418                 :            :  * tuples with space for an OID, though we really only need the topmost node
    2419                 :            :  * to do so.  However, node types like Sort don't project new tuples but just
    2420                 :            :  * return their inputs, and in those cases the requirement propagates down
    2421                 :            :  * to the input node.  Eventually we might make this code smart enough to
    2422                 :            :  * recognize how far down the requirement really goes, but for now we just
    2423                 :            :  * make all plan nodes do the same thing if the top level forces the choice.
    2424                 :            :  *
    2425                 :            :  * We assume that estate->es_result_relation_info is already set up to
    2426                 :            :  * describe the target relation.  Note that in an UPDATE that spans an
    2427                 :            :  * inheritance tree, some of the target relations may have OIDs and some not.
    2428                 :            :  * We have to make the decisions on a per-relation basis as we initialize
    2429                 :            :  * each of the child plans of the topmost Append plan.
    2430                 :            :  *
    2431                 :            :  * SELECT INTO is even uglier, because we don't have the INTO relation's
    2432                 :            :  * descriptor available when this code runs; we have to look aside at a
    2433                 :            :  * flag set by InitPlan().
    2434                 :            :  */

    5381                 :            : /* Check compatibility of the attributes of the given partitioned
    5382                 :            :  * table and part for purposes of INSERT (through the partitioned
    5383                 :            :  * table) or EXCHANGE (of the part into the partitioned table).
    5384                 :            :  * Don't use any partitioning catalogs, because this must run
    5385                 :            :  * on the segment databases as well as on the entry database.
    5386                 :            :  *
    5387                 :            :  * If requested and needed, make a vector mapping the attribute
    5388                 :            :  * numbers of the partitioned table to corresponding attribute 
    5389                 :            :  * numbers in the part.  Represent the "unneeded" identity map
    5390                 :            :  * as null.
    5391                 :            :  *
    5392                 :            :  * base -- the partitioned table
    5393                 :            :  * part -- the part table
    5394                 :            :  * map_ptr -- where to store a pointer to the result, or NULL
    5395                 :            :  * throw -- whether to throw an error in case of incompatibility
    5396                 :            :  *
    5397                 :            :  * The implicit result is a vector one longer than the number
    5398                 :            :  * of attributes (existing or not) in the base relation.
    5399                 :            :  * It is returned through the map_ptr argument, if that argument
    5400                 :            :  * is non-null.
    5401                 :            :  *
    5402                 :            :  * The explicit result indicates whether the part is compatible
    5403                 :            :  * with the base relation.  If the throw argument is true, however,
    5404                 :            :  * an error is issued rather than returning false.
    5405                 :            :  *
    5406                 :            :  * Note that, in the map, element 0 is wasted and is always zero, 
    5407                 :            :  * so the vector is indexed by attribute number (origin 1).
    5408                 :            :  *
    5409                 :            :  * The i-th element of the map is the attribute number in 
    5410                 :            :  * the part relation that corresponds to attribute i of the  
    5411                 :            :  * base relation, or it is zero to indicate that attribute 
    5412                 :            :  * i of the base relation doesn't exist (has been dropped).
    5413                 :            :  *
    5414                 :            :  * This is a handy map for renumbering attributes for use with
    5415                 :            :  * part relations that may have a different configuration of 
    5416                 :            :  * "holes" than the partitioned table in which they occur.
    5417                 :            :  * 
    5418                 :            :  * Be sure to call this in the memory context in which the result
    5419                 :            :  * vector ought to be stored.
    5420                 :            :  *
    5421                 :            :  * Though some error checking is done, it is not comprehensive.
    5422                 :            :  * If internal assumptions about possible tuple formats are
    5423                 :            :  * correct, errors should not occur.  Still, the downside is
    5424                 :            :  * incorrect data, so use errors (not assertions) for the case.
    5425                 :            :  *
    5426                 :            :  * Checks include same number of non-dropped attributes in all 
    5427                 :            :  * parts of a partitioned table, non-dropped attributes in 
    5428                 :            :  * corresponding relative positions must match in name, type
    5429                 :            :  * and alignment, attribute numbers must agree with their
    5430                 :            :  * position in tuple, etc.
